container-lg\" itemprop=\"text\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-gguf\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: GGUF\" href=\"#gguf\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF is a file format for storing models for inference with GGML and executors based on GGML. GGUF is a binary format that is designed for fast loading and saving of models, and for ease of reading. Models are traditionally developed using PyTorch or another framework, and then converted to GGUF for use in GGML.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt is a successor file format to GGML, GGMF and GGJT, and is designed to be unambiguous by containing all the information needed to load a model. It is also designed to be extensible, so that new information can be added to models without breaking compatibility.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor more information about the motivation behind GGUF, see \u003ca href=\"#historical-state-of-affairs\"\u003eHistorical State of Affairs\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSpecification\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-specification\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Specification\" href=\"#specification\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF is a format based on the existing GGJT, but makes a few changes to the format to make it more extensible and easier to use. The following features are desired:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSingle-file deployment: they can be easily distributed and loaded, and do not require any external files for additional information.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eExtensible: new features can be added to GGML-based executors/new information can be added to GGUF models without breaking compatibility with existing models.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emmap\u003c/code\u003e compatibility: models can be loaded using \u003ccode\u003emmap\u003c/code\u003e for fast loading and saving.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eEasy to use: models can be easily loaded and saved using a small amount of code, with no need for external libraries, regardless of the language used.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eFull information: all information needed to load a model is contained in the model file, and no additional information needs to be provided by the user.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe key difference between GGJT and GGUF is the use of a key-value structure for the hyperparameters (now referred to as metadata), rather than a list of untyped values. This allows for new metadata to be added without breaking compatibility with existing models, and to annotate the model with additional information that may be useful for inference or for identifying the model.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF Naming Convention\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-gguf-naming-convention\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: GGUF Naming Convention\" href=\"#gguf-naming-convention\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF follow a naming convention of \u003ccode\u003e[\u0026lt;Sidecar\u0026gt;]\u0026lt;BaseName\u0026gt;\u0026lt;SizeLabel\u0026gt;\u0026lt;FineTune\u0026gt;\u0026lt;Version\u0026gt;\u0026lt;Encoding\u0026gt;\u0026lt;Type\u0026gt;\u0026lt;Shard\u0026gt;.gguf\u003c/code\u003e where each component is delimitated by a \u003ccode\u003e-\u003c/code\u003e if present. Ultimately this is intended to make it easier for humans to at a glance get the most important details of a model. It is not intended to be perfectly parsable in the field due to the diversity of existing gguf filenames.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe components are:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSidecar\u003c/strong\u003e: (Optional) Prefix marking the file as an auxiliary module loaded alongside a base model, rather than a standalone model. When present, sits at the very front of the filename followed by \u003ccode\u003e-\u003c/code\u003e. Lowercase by convention.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emmproj\u003c/code\u003e : Multimodal projector (vision/audio encoder and projection layer for use with a base LLM)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emtp\u003c/code\u003e : Multi-Token Prediction heads (speculative-decoding draft module, intended to be loaded alongside a base model of matching architecture and version). Note that oftentimes the MTP weights can be distributed inside the base model, in which case there is no separate \u003ccode\u003emtp-\u003c/code\u003e sidecar file.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eBaseName\u003c/strong\u003e: A descriptive name for the model base type or architecture.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThis can be derived from gguf metadata \u003ccode\u003egeneral.basename\u003c/code\u003e substituting spaces for dashes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSizeLabel\u003c/strong\u003e: Parameter weight class (useful for leader boards) represented as \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;expertCount\u0026gt;x\u0026lt;count\u0026gt;\u0026lt;scale-prefix\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThis can be derived from gguf metadata \u003ccode\u003egeneral.size_label\u003c/code\u003e if available or calculated if missing.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRounded decimal point is supported in count with a single letter scale prefix to assist in floating point exponent shown below\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eQ\u003c/code\u003e: Quadrillion parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eT\u003c/code\u003e: Trillion parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eB\u003c/code\u003e: Billion parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eM\u003c/code\u003e: Million parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eK\u003c/code\u003e: Thousand parameters.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdditional \u003ccode\u003e-\u0026lt;attributes\u0026gt;\u0026lt;count\u0026gt;\u0026lt;scale-prefix\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e can be appended as needed to indicate other attributes of interest\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFineTune\u003c/strong\u003e: A descriptive name for the model fine tuning goal (e.g. Chat, Instruct, etc...)\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThis can be derived from gguf metadata \u003ccode\u003egeneral.finetune\u003c/code\u003e substituting spaces for dashes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eVersion\u003c/strong\u003e: (Optional) Denotes the model version number, formatted as \u003ccode\u003ev\u0026lt;Major\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;Minor\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf model is missing a version number then assume \u003ccode\u003ev1.0\u003c/code\u003e (First Public Release)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThis can be derived from gguf metadata \u003ccode\u003egeneral.version\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eEncoding\u003c/strong\u003e: Indicates the weights encoding scheme that was applied to the model. Content, type mixture and arrangement however are determined by user code and can vary depending on project needs.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eType\u003c/strong\u003e: Indicates the kind of gguf file and the intended purpose for it\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf missing, then file is by default a typical gguf tensor model file\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eLoRA\u003c/code\u003e : GGUF file is a LoRA adapter\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003evocab\u003c/code\u003e : GGUF file with only vocab data and metadata\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eShard\u003c/strong\u003e: (Optional) Indicates and denotes that the model has been split into multiple shards, formatted as \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;ShardNum\u0026gt;-of-\u0026lt;ShardTotal\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eShardNum\u003c/em\u003e : Shard position in this model. Must be 5 digits padded by zeros.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eShard number always starts from \u003ccode\u003e00001\u003c/code\u003e onwards (e.g. First shard always starts at \u003ccode\u003e00001-of-XXXXX\u003c/code\u003e rather than \u003ccode\u003e00000-of-XXXXX\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eShardTotal\u003c/em\u003e : Total number of shards in this model. Must be 5 digits padded by zeros.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eValidating Above Naming Convention\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-validating-above-naming-convention\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Validating Above Naming Convention\" href=\"#validating-above-naming-convention\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAt a minimum all model files should have at least BaseName, SizeLabel, Version, in order to be easily validated as a file that is keeping with the GGUF Naming Convention. An example of this issue is that it is easy for Encoding to be mistaken as a FineTune if Version is omitted.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo validate you can use this regular expression \u003ccode\u003e^(?:(?\u0026lt;Sidecar\u0026gt;mmproj|mtp)-)?(?\u0026lt;BaseName\u0026gt;[A-Za-z0-9\\s]*(?:(?:-(?:(?:[A-Za-z\\s][A-Za-z0-9\\s]*)|(?:[0-9\\s]*)))*))-(?:(?\u0026lt;SizeLabel\u0026gt;(?:\\d+x)?(?:\\d+\\.)?\\d+[A-Za-z](?:-[A-Za-z]+(\\d+\\.)?\\d+[A-Za-z]+)?)(?:-(?\u0026lt;FineTune\u0026gt;[A-Za-z0-9\\s-]+))?)?-(?:(?\u0026lt;Version\u0026gt;v\\d+(?:\\.\\d+)*))(?:-(?\u0026lt;Encoding\u0026gt;(?!LoRA|vocab)[\\w_]+))?(?:-(?\u0026lt;Type\u0026gt;LoRA|vocab))?(?:-(?\u0026lt;Shard\u0026gt;\\d{5}-of-\\d{5}))?\\.gguf$\u003c/code\u003e which will check that you got the minimum BaseName, SizeLabel and Version present in the correct order.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eMixtral-8x7B-v0.1-KQ2.gguf\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eModel Name: Mixtral\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eExpert Count: 8\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eParameter Count: 7B\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVersion Number: v0.1\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWeight Encoding Scheme: KQ2\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eHermes-2-Pro-Llama-3-8B-F16.gguf\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul Number: v1.0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWeight Encoding Scheme: F16\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eShard: N/A\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eGrok-100B-v1.0-Q4_0-00003-of-00009.gguf\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eModel Name: Grok\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eExpert Count: 0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eParameter Count: 100B\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVersion Number: v1.0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWeight Encoding dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003emtp-Qwen3-27B-v1.0-Q4_K_M.gguf\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSidecar: mtp (Multi-Token Prediction draft module)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eModel Name: Qwen3\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eExpert Count: 0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eParameter Count: 27B (of the main model — sidecar tensors are projector)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eModel Name: Qwen2-VL\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eExpert Count: 0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eParameter Count: 7B (of the main model — sidecar tensors are smaller)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVersion Number: v1.0\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWeight Encoding Scheme: F16\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdetails\u003e\u003csummary\u003eExample Node.js Regex Function\u003c/summary\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"#!/usr/bin/env node\nconst ggufRegex = /^(?:(?\u0026lt;Sidecar\u0026gt;mmproj|mtp)-)?(?\u0026lt;BaseName\u0026gt;[A-Za-z0-9\\s]*(?:(?:-(?:(?:[A-Za-z\\s][A-Za-z0-9\\s]*)|(?:[0-9\\s]*)))*))-(?:(?\u0026lt;SizeLabel\u0026gt;(?:\\d+x)?(?:\\d+\\.)?\\d+[A-Za-z](?:-[A-Za-z]+(\\d+\\.)?\\d+[A-Za-z]+)?)(?:-(?\u0026lt;FineTune\u0026gt;[A-Za-z0-9\\s-]+))?)?-(?:(?\u0026lt;Version\u0026gt;v\\d+(?:\\.\\d+)*))(?:-(?\u0026lt;Encoding\u0026gt;(?!LoRA|vocab)[\\w_]+))?(?:-(?\u0026lt;Type\u0026gt;LoRA|vocab))?(?:-(?\u0026lt;Shard\u0026gt;\\d{5}-of-\\d{5}))?\\.gguf$/;\n\nfunction parseGGUFFilename(filename) {\n  const match = ggufRegex.exec(filename);\n  if (!match)\n    return null;\n  const {Sidecar = null, BaseName = null, SizeLabel = null, FineTune = null, Version = \u0026quot;v1.0\u0026quot;, Encoding = null, Type = null, Shard = null} = match.groups;\n  return {Sidecar: Sidecar, BaseName: BaseName, SizeLabel: SizeLabel, FineTune: FineTune, Version: Version, Encoding: Encoding, Type: Type, Shard: Shard};\n}\n\nconst testCases = [\n  {filename: 'Mixtral-8x7B-v0.1-KQ2.gguf',                         expected: { Sidecar: null,   BaseName: 'Mixtral',              SizeLabel: '8x7B',     FineTune: null, Version: 'v0.1',   Encoding: 'KQ2',    Type: null, Shard: null}},\n  {filename: 'Grok-100B-v1.0-Q4_0-00003-of-00009.gguf',            expected: { Sidecar: null,   BaseName: 'Grok',                 SizeLabel: '100B',     FineTune: null, Version: 'v1.0',   Encoding: 'Q4_0',   Type: null, Shard: \u0026quot;00003-of-00009\u0026quot;}},\n  {filename: 'Hermes-2-Pro-Llama-3-8B-v1.0-F16.gguf',              expected: { Sidecar: null,   BaseName: 'Hermes-2-Pro-Llama-3', SizeLabel: '8B',       FineTune: null, Version: 'v1.0',   Encoding: 'F16',    Type: null, Shard: null}},\n  {filename: 'Phi-3-mini-3.8B-ContextLength4k-instruct-v1.0.gguf', expected: { Sidecar: null,   BaseName: 'Phi-3-mini',           SizeLabel: '3.8B-ContextLength4k', FineTune: 'instruct', Version: 'v1.0', Encoding: null,    Type: null, Shard: null}},\n  {filename: 'mtp-Qwen3-27B-v1.0-Q4_K_M.gguf',                     expected: { Sidecar: 'mtp',  BaseName: 'Qwen3',                SizeLabel: '27B',      FineTune: null, Version: 'v1.0',   Encoding: 'Q4_K_M', Type: null, Shard: null}},\n  {filename: 'mmproj-Qwen2-VL-7B-v1.0-F16.gguf',                   expected: { Sidecar: 'mmproj', BaseName: 'Qwen2-VL',           SizeLabel: '7B',       FineTune: null, Version: 'v1.0',   Encoding: 'F16',    Type: null, Shard: null}},\n  {filename: 'not-a-known-arrangement.gguf',                       expected: null},\n];\n\ntestCases.forEach(({ filename, expected }) =\u0026gt; {\n  const result = parseGGUFFilename(filename);\n  const passed = JSON.stringify(result) === JSON.stringify(expected);\n  console.log(`${filename}: ${passed ? \u0026quot;PASS\u0026quot; : \u0026quot;FAIL\u0026quot;}`);\n  if (!passed) {\n      console.log(result);\n      console.log(expected);\n  }\n});\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e#!/usr/bin/env node\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003econst\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eggufRegex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan alt=\"image\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\n\u003cem\u003ediagram by \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/mishig25\"\u003e@mishig25\u003c/a\u003e (GGUF v3)\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGUF files are structured as follows. They use a global alignment specified in the \u003ccode\u003egeneral.alignment\u003c/code\u003e metadata field, referred to as \u003ccode\u003eALIGNMENT\u003c/code\u003e below. Where required, the file is padded with \u003ccode\u003e0x00\u003c/code\u003e bytes to the next multiple of \u003ccode\u003egeneral.alignment\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFields, including arrays, are written sequentially without alignment unless otherwise specified.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eModels are little-endian by default. They can also come in big-endian for use with big-endian computers; in this case, all values (including metadata values and tensors) will also be big-endian. At the time of writing, there is no way to determine if a model is big-endian; this may be rectified in future versions. If no additional information is provided, assume the model is little-endian.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"enum ggml_type: uint32_t {\n    GGML_TYPE_F32     = 0,\n    GGML_TYPE_F16     = 1,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q4_0    = 2,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q4_1    = 3,\n    // GGML_TYPE_Q4_2 = 4, support has been removed\n    // GGML_TYPE_Q4_3 = 5, support has been removed\n    GGML_TYPE_Q5_0    = 6,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q5_1    = 7,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q8_0    = 8,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q8_1    = 9,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q2_K    = 10,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q3_K    = 11,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q4_K    = 12,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q5_K    = 13,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q6_K    = 14,\n    GGML_TYPE_Q8_K    = 15,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ2_XXS = 16,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ2_XS  = 17,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ3_XXS = 18,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ1_S   = 19,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ4_NL  = 20,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ3_S   = 21,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ2_S   = 22,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ4_XS  = 23,\n    GGML_TYPE_I8      = 24,\n    GGML_TYPE_I16     = 25,\n    GGML_TYPE_I32     = 26,\n    GGML_TYPE_I64     = 27,\n    GGML_TYPE_F64     = 28,\n    GGML_TYPE_IQ1_M   = 29,\n    GGML_TYPE_BF16    = 30,\n    // GGML_TYPE_Q4_0_4_4 = 31, support has been removed from gguf files\n    // GGML_TYPE_Q4_0_4_8 = 32,\n    // GGML_TYPE_Q4_0_8_8 = 33,\n    GGML_TYPE_TQ1_0   = 34,\n    GGML_TYPE_TQ2_0   = 35,\n    // GGML_TYPE_IQ4_NL_4_4 = 36,\n    // GGML_TYPE_IQ4_NL_4_8 = 37,\n    // GGML_TYPE_IQ4_NL_8_8 = 38,\n    GGML_TYPE_MXFP4   = 39, // MXFP4 (1 block)\n    GGML_TYPE_COUNT   = 40,\n};\n\nenum gguf_metadata_value_type: uint32_t {\n    // The value is a 8-bit unsigned integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_UINT8 = 0,\n    // The value is a 8-bit signed integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_INT8 = 1,\n    // The value is a 16-bit unsigned little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_UINT16 = 2,\n    // The value is a 16-bit signed little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_INT16 = 3,\n    // The value is a 32-bit unsigned little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_UINT32 = 4,\n    // The value is a 32-bit signed little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_INT32 = 5,\n    // The value is a 32-bit IEEE754 floating point number.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_FLOAT32 = 6,\n    // The value is a boolean.\n    // 1-byte value where 0 is false and 1 is true.\n    // Anything else is invalid, and should be treated as either the model being invalid or the reader being buggy.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_BOOL = 7,\n    // The value is a UTF-8 non-null-terminated string, with length prepended.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_STRING = 8,\n    // The value is an array of other values, with the length and type prepended.\n    ///\n    // Arrays can be nested, and the length of the array is the number of elements in the array, not the number of bytes.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_ARRAY = 9,\n    // The value is a 64-bit unsigned little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_UINT64 = 10,\n    // The value is a 64-bit signed little-endian integer.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_INT64 = 11,\n    // The value is a 64-bit IEEE754 floating point number.\n    GGUF_METADATA_VALUE_TYPE_FLOAT64 = 12,\n};\n\n// A string in GGUF.\nstruct gguf_string_t {\n    // The length of the string, in bytes.\n    uint64_t len;\n    // The string as a UTF-8 non-null-terminated string.\n    char string[len];\n};\n\nunion gguf_metadata_value_t {\n    uint8_t uint8;\n    int8_t int8;\n    uint16_t uint16;\n    int16_t int16;\n    uint32_t uint32;\n    int32_t int32;\n    float float32;\n    uint64_t uint64;\n    int64_t int64;\n    double float64;\n    bool bool_;\n    gguf_string_t string;\n    struct {\n        // Any value type is valid, including arrays.\n        gguf_metadata_value_type type;\n        // Number of elements, not bytes\n        uint64_t len;\n        // The array of values.\n        gguf_metadata_value_t array[len];\n    } array;\n};\n\nstruct gguf_metadata_kv_t {\n    // The key of the metadata. It is a standard GGUF string, with the following caveats:\n    // - It must be a valid ASCII string.\n    // - It must be a hierarchical key, where each segment is `lower_snake_case` and separated by a `.`.\n    // - It must be at most 2^16-1/65535 bytes long.\n    // Any keys that do not follow these rules are invalid.\n    gguf_string_t key;\n\n    // The type of the value.\n    // Must be one of the `gguf_metadata_value_type` values.\n    gguf_metadata_value_type value_type;\n    // The value.\n    gguf_metadata_value_t value;\n};\n\nstruct gguf_header_t {\n    // Magic number to announce that this is a GGUF file.\n    // Must be `GGUF` at the byte level: `0x47` `0x47` `0x55` `0x46`.\n    // Your executor might do little-endian byte order, so it might be\n    // check for 0x46554747 and letting the endianness cancel out.\n    // Consider being *very* explicit about the byte order here.\n    uint32_t magic;\n    // The version of the format implemented.\n    // Must be `3` for version described in this spec, which introduces big-endian support.\n    //\n    // This version should only be increased for structural changes to the format.\n    // Changes that do not affect the structure of the file should instead update the metadata\n    // to signify the change.\n    uint32_t version;\n    // The number of tensors in the file.\n    // This is explicit, instead of being included in the metadata, to ensure it is always present\n    // for loading the tensors.\n    uint64_t tensor_count;\n    // The number of metadata key-value pairs.\n    uint64_t metadata_kv_count;\n    // The metadata key-value pairs.\n    gguf_metadata_kv_t metadata_kv[metadata_kv_count];\n};\n\nuint64_t align_offset(uint64_t offset) {\n    return offset + (ALIGNMENT - (offset % ALIGNMENT)) % ALIGNMENT;\n}\n\nstruct gguf_tensor_info_t {\n    // The name of the tensor. It is a standard GGUF string, with the caveat that\n    // it must be at most 64 bytes long.\n    gguf_string_t name;\n    // The number of dimensions in the tensor.\n    // Currently at most 4, but this may change in the future.\n    uint32_t n_dimensions;\n    // The dimensions of the tensor.\n    uint64_t dimensions[n_dimensions];\n    // The type of the tensor.\n    ggml_type type;\n    // The offset of the tensor's data in this file in bytes.\n    //\n    // This offset is relative to `tensor_data`, not to the start\n    // of the file, to make it easier for writers to write the file.\n    // Readers should consider exposing this offset relative to the\n    // file to make it easier to read the data.\n    //\n    // Must be a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`. That is, `align_offset(offset) == offset`.\n    uint64_t offset;\n};\n\nstruct gguf_file_t {\n    // The header of the file.\n    gguf_header_t header;\n\n    // Tensor infos, which can be used to locate the tensor data.\n    gguf_tensor_info_t tensor_infos[header.tensor_count];\n\n    // Padding to the nearest multiple of `ALIGNMENT`.\n    //\n    // That is, if `sizeof(header) + sizeof(tensor_infos)` is not a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`,\n    // this padding is added to make it so.\n    //\n    // This can be calculated as `align_offset(position) - position`, where `position` is\n    // the position of the end of `tensor_infos` (i.e. `sizeof(header) + sizeof(tensor_infos)`).\n    uint8_t _padding[];\n\n    // Tensor data.\n    //\n    // This is arbitrary binary data corresponding to the weights of the model. This data should be close\n    // or identical to the data in the original model file, but may be different due to quantization or\n    // other optimizations for inference. Any such deviations should be recorded in the metadata or as\n    // part of the architecture definition.\n    //\n    // Each tensor's data must be stored within this array, and located through its `tensor_infos` entry.\n    // The offset of each tensor's data must be a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`, and the space between tensors\n    // should be padded to `ALIGNMENT` bytes.\n    uint8_t tensor_data[];\n};\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eenum\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eggml_type\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_metadata_kv_t\u003c/span\u003e {\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The key of the metadata. class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Magic number to announce that this is a GGUF file.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Must be `GGUF` at the byte level: `0x47` `0x47` `0x55` class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_tensor_info_t\u003c/span\u003e {\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The name of the tensor. It is a standard GGUF string, with the caveat that\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// it must be at most 64 bytes long.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_string_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e;\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The number of dimensions in the tensor.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Currently at most 4, but this may change in the future.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003euint32_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003en_dimensions\u003c/span\u003e;\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The dimensions of the tensor.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003euint64_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003edimensions\u003c/span\u003e[\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en_dimensions\u003c/span\u003e];\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The type of the tensor.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003eggml_type\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etype\u003c/span\u003e;\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The offset of the tensor's data in this file in bytes.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// This offset is relative to `tensor_data`, not to the start\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// of the file, to make it easier for writers to write the file.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Readers should consider exposing this offset relative to the\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// file to make it easier to read the data.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Must be a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`. That is, `align_offset(offset) == offset`.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003euint64_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eoffset\u003c/span\u003e;\n};\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003estruct\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_file_t\u003c/span\u003e {\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The header of the file.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_header_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eheader\u003c/span\u003e;\n\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Tensor infos, which can be used to locate the tensor data.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003egguf_tensor_info_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etensor_infos\u003c/span\u003e[\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eheader\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etensor_count\u003c/span\u003e];\n\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Padding to the nearest multiple of `ALIGNMENT`.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// That is, if `sizeof(header) + sizeof(tensor_infos)` is not a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`,\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// this padding is added to make it so.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// This can be calculated as `align_offset(position) - position`, where `position` is\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// the position of the end of `tensor_infos` (i.e. `sizeof(header) + sizeof(tensor_infos)`).\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003euint8_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e_padding\u003c/span\u003e[];\n\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Tensor data.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// This is arbitrary binary data corresponding to the weights of the model. This data should be close\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// or identical to the data in the original model file, but may be different due to quantization or\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// other optimizations for inference. Any such deviations should be recorded in the metadata or as\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// part of the architecture definition.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// Each tensor's data must be stored within this array, and located through its `tensor_infos` entry.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// The offset of each tensor's data must be a multiple of `ALIGNMENT`, and the space between tensors\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// should be padded to `ALIGNMENT` bytes.\u003c/span\u003e\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003euint8_t\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etensor_data\u003c/span\u003e[];\n};\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eStandardized key-value pairs\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-standardized-key-value-pairs\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Standardized key-value pairs\" href=\"#standardized-key-value-pairs\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following key-value pairs are standardized. This list may grow in the future as more use cases are discovered. Where possible, names are shared with the original model definitions to make it easier to map between the two.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNot all of these are required, but they are all recommended. Keys that are required are bolded. For omitted pairs, the reader should assume that the value is unknown and either default or error as appropriate.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe community can develop their own key-value pairs to carry additional data. However, these should be namespaced with the relevant community name to avoid collisions. For example, the \u003ccode\u003erustformers\u003c/code\u003e community might use \u003ccode\u003erustformers.\u003c/code\u003e as a prefix for all of their keys.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf a particular community key is widely used, it may be promoted to a standardized key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBy convention, most counts/lengths/etc are \u003ccode\u003euint64\u003c/code\u003e unless otherwise specified. This is to allow for larger models to be supported in the future. Some models may use \u003ccode\u003euint32\u003c/code\u003e for their values; it is recommended that readers support both.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" (Useful for leader boards)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egeneral.license: string\u003c/code\u003e: License of the model, expressed as a \u003ca href=\"https://spdx.github.io/spdx-spec/v2-draft/SPDX-license-expressions/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eSPDX license expression\u003c/a\u003e (e.g. \u003ccode\u003e\"MIT OR Apache-2.0\u003c/code\u003e). Do not include any other information, such as the license text or the URL to the license.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egeneral.license.name: string\u003c/code\u003e: Human friendly license name\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egeneral.license.link: string\u003c/code\u003e: URL to the license.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egeneral.url: string\u003c/code\u003e: URL to the model's homepage. This is useful for tracking the provenance of the model, and for finding the original source if the model is modified. For a model that was converted from GGML, for example, these keys would point to the model that was converted from.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egeneral.source.url: string\u003c/code\u003e: URL to the source of the model's homepage. specific LLM architecture. For example, \u003ccode\u003ellama\u003c/code\u003e for LLaMA, \u003ccode\u003empt\u003c/code\u003e for MPT, etc. If mentioned in an architecture's section, it is required for that architecture, but not all keys are required for all architectures. Consult the relevant section for more information.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[llm].context_length: uint64\u003c/code\u003e: Also known as \u003ccode\u003en_ctx\u003c/code\u003e. length of the context (in tokens) that the model was trained on. For most architectures, this is the hard limit on the length of the input. Architectures, like RWKV, that are not reliant on transformer-style attention may be able to handle larger inputs, but this is not guaranteed.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[llm].embedding_length: uint64\u003c/code\u003e: Also known as \u003ccode\u003en_embd\u003c/code\u003e. Does not include the input or embedding layers.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[llm].feed_forward_length: uint64\u003c/code\u003e: Also known as \u003ccode\u003en_ff\u003c/code\u003e. This key describes the layout of the tensor data. This is not required; if not present, it is assumed to be \u003ccode\u003ereference\u003c/code\u003e.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ereference\u003c/code\u003e: tensors are laid out in the same order as the original model\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003efurther options can be found for each architecture in their respective sections\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[llm].expert_count: uint32\u003c/code\u003e: Number of experts in MoE models (optional for non-MoE arches).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[llm].expert_used_count: uint32\u003c/code\u003e: Number of experts used during each token token evaluation (optional for non-MoE arches).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eAttention\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-attention\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Attention\" href=\"#attention\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003ccode\u003e[llm].attention.head_count: uint64\u003c/code\u003e: Also known as \u003ccode\u003en_head\u003c/code\u003e. dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003efalcon.tensor_data_layout\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejploski\u003c/code\u003e (author of the original GGML implementation of Falcon):\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# The original query_key_value tensor contains n_head_kv \u0026quot;kv groups\u0026quot;,\n# each consisting of n_head/n_head_kv query weights followed by one key\n# and one value weight (shared by all query heads in the kv group).\n# This layout makes it a big pain to work with in GGML.\n# So we rearrange them here,, so that we have n_head query weights\n# followed by n_head_kv key weights followed by n_head_kv value weights,\n# in contiguous fashion.\n\nif \u0026quot;query_key_value\u0026quot; in src:\n    qkv = model[src].view(\n        n_head_kv, n_head // n_head_kv + 2, head_dim, head_dim * n_head)\n\n    q = qkv[:, :-2 ].reshape(n_head * head_dim, head_dim * n_head)\n    k = qkv[:, [-2]].reshape(n_head_kv * head_dim, head_dim * n_head)\n    v = qkv[:, [-1]].reshape(n_head_kv * head_dim, head_dim * n_head)\n\n    model[src] = torch.cat((q,k,v)).reshape_as(model[src])\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# The original query_key_value tensor contains n_head_kv \"kv groups\",\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan When a more accurate tokenizer is available and supported, it should be used instead.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt is not guaranteed to be standardized across models, and may change in the future. It is recommended that model authors use a more standardized tokenizer if possible.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etokenizer.ggml.model: string\u003c/code\u003e: The name of the tokenizer model.\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ellama\u003c/code\u003e: Llama style SentencePiece (tokens and scores extracted from HF \u003ccode\u003etokenizer.model\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ereplit\u003c/code\u003e: Replit style SentencePiece (tokens and scores extracted from HF \u003ccode\u003espiece.model\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egpt2\u003c/code\u003e: GPT-2 / GPT-NeoX style BPE (tokens extracted from HF \u003ccode\u003etokenizer.json\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003erwkv\u003c/code\u003e: RWKV tokenizer\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etokenizer.ggml.tokens: array[string]\u003c/code\u003e: A list of tokens indexed by the token ID used by the model.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etokenizer.ggml.scores: array[float32]\u003c/code\u003e: If present, the score/probability of each token. If present, it must have the same length and index as \u003ccode\u003etokens\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etokenizer.ggml.token_type: array[int32]\u003c/code\u003e: The token type (1=normal, 2=unknown, 3=control, 4=user defined, 5=unused, 6=byte). If present, it must have the same length and index as \u003ccode\u003etokens\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etokenizer.ggml.merges: array[string]\u003c/code\u003e: If present, the merges of the tokenizer. provided for context, but is not necessary to understand the rest of this document.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eOverview\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-overview\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Overview\" href=\"#overview\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAt present, there are three GGML file formats floating around for LLMs:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGGML\u003c/strong\u003e (unversioned): baseline format, with no versioning or alignment.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGGMF\u003c/strong\u003e (versioned): the same as GGML, but with versioning. Only one version exists.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGGJT\u003c/strong\u003e: Aligns the tensors to allow for use with \u003ccode\u003emmap\u003c/code\u003e, which requires alignment. v1, v2 and v3 are identical, but the latter versions use a different quantization scheme that is incompatible with previous versions.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGGML is primarily used by the examples in \u003ccode\u003eggml\u003c/code\u003e, while GGJT is used by \u003ccode\u003ellama.cpp\u003c/code\u003e models. Other executors may use any of the three formats, but this is not 'officially' supported.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThese formats share the same fundamental structure:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea magic number with an optional version number\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003emodel-specific hyperparameters, including\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003emetadata about the model, such as the number of layers, the number of heads, etc.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ea \u003ccode\u003eftype\u003c/code\u003e that describes the type of the majority of the tensors,\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003efor GGML files, the quantization version is encoded in the \u003ccode\u003eftype\u003c/code\u003e divided by 1000\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ean embedded vocabulary, which is a list of strings with length prepended. The GGMF/GGJT formats embed a float32 score next to the strings.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003efinally, a list of tensors with their length-prepended name, type, and (aligned, in the case of GGJT) tensor data\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNotably, this structure does not identify what model architecture the model belongs to, nor does it offer any flexibility for changing the structure of the hyperparameters. This means that the only way to add new hyperparameters is to add them to the end of the list, which is a breaking change for existing models.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDrawbacks\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-drawbacks\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Drawbacks\" href=\"#drawbacks\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUnfortunately, over the last few months, there are a few issues that have become apparent with the existing models:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThere's no way to identify which model architecture a given model is for, because that information isn't present\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSimilarly, existing programs cannot intelligently fail upon encountering new architectures\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding or removing any new hyperparameters is a breaking change, which is impossible for a reader to detect without using heuristics\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eEach model architecture requires its own conversion script to their architecture's variant of GGML\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eMaintaining backwards compatibility without breaking the structure of the format requires clever tricks, like packing the quantization version into the ftype, which are not guaranteed to be picked up by readers/writers, and are not consistent between the two formats\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy not other formats?\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-not-other-formats\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why not other formats?\" href=\"#why-not-other-formats\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere are a few other formats that could be used, but issues include:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003erequiring additional dependencies to load or save the model, which is complicated in a C environment\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003elimited or no support for 4-bit quantization\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eexisting cultural expectations (e.g. whether or not the model is a directory or a file)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003elack of support for embedded vocabularies\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003elack of control over direction of future development\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUltimately, it is likely that GGUF will
